					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American rapper and actor (born 1971)</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Snoopy" title="Snoopy">Snoopy</a>.</div>

<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://snoopdogg.com">snoopdogg<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Calvin Cordozar Broadus Jr.</b> (born October 20, 1971), known professionally as <b>Snoop Dogg</b> (previously <b>Snoop Doggy Dogg</b> and briefly <b>Snoop Lion</b>),<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> is an American rapper and actor. His fame dates back to 1992 when he was featured on <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>'s debut solo single, "<a href="/wiki/Deep_Cover_(song)" title="Deep Cover (song)">Deep Cover</a>", and then on Dre's debut solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chronic" title="The Chronic">The Chronic</a></i>. Broadus has since sold over 23 million albums in the United States and 35 million albums worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Snoop_Dogg" title="List of awards and nominations received by Snoop Dogg">His accolades</a> include an <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Award</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Awards" title="Primetime Emmy Awards">Primetime Emmy Award</a>, and 17 nominations at the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a>.
</p><p>Broadus' debut solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Doggystyle" title="Doggystyle">Doggystyle</a>,</i> produced by Dr. Dre, was released by <a href="/wiki/Death_Row_Records" title="Death Row Records">Death Row Records</a> in November 1993, and debuted at number one on the popular albums chart, the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, and on <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a> chart. Selling 800,000 copies in its first week, <i>Doggystyle</i> was <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">certified</a> quadruple-platinum in 1994 and featured the singles "<a href="/wiki/What%27s_My_Name%3F_(Snoop_Doggy_Dogg_song)" title="What&#39;s My Name? (Snoop Doggy Dogg song)">What's My Name?</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Gin_and_Juice" title="Gin and Juice">Gin and Juice</a>". In 1994, Death Row Records released a soundtrack, by Broadus, for the short film <i><a href="/wiki/Murder_Was_the_Case" title="Murder Was the Case">Murder Was the Case</a>,</i> starring Snoop. In 1996, his second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Doggfather" title="Tha Doggfather">Tha Doggfather</a>,</i> also debuted at number one on both charts, with "<a href="/wiki/Snoop%27s_Upside_Ya_Head" title="Snoop&#39;s Upside Ya Head">Snoop's Upside Ya Head</a>" as the lead single. The next year, the album was certified double-platinum.
</p><p>After leaving Death Row Records in January 1998, Broadus signed with <a href="/wiki/No_Limit_Records" title="No Limit Records">No Limit Records</a>, releasing three albums: <i><a href="/wiki/Da_Game_Is_to_Be_Sold,_Not_to_Be_Told" title="Da Game Is to Be Sold, Not to Be Told">Da Game Is to Be Sold, Not to Be Told</a></i> (1998), <i><a href="/wiki/No_Limit_Top_Dogg" title="No Limit Top Dogg">No Limit Top Dogg</a></i> (1999), and <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Last_Meal" title="Tha Last Meal">Tha Last Meal</a></i> (2000). In 2002, he signed with <a href="/wiki/Priority_Records" title="Priority Records">Priority</a>/<a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol</a>/<a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a> Records, releasing <i><a href="/wiki/Paid_tha_Cost_to_Be_da_Boss" title="Paid tha Cost to Be da Boss">Paid tha Cost to Be da Boss</a></i>. In 2004, he signed to <a href="/wiki/Geffen_Records" title="Geffen Records">Geffen Records</a>, releasing his next three albums: <i><a href="/wiki/R%26G_(Rhythm_%26_Gangsta):_The_Masterpiece" title="R&amp;G (Rhythm &amp; Gangsta): The Masterpiece">R&amp;G (Rhythm &amp; Gangsta): The Masterpiece</a>,</i> then <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Blue_Carpet_Treatment" title="Tha Blue Carpet Treatment">Tha Blue Carpet Treatment</a>,</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ego_Trippin%27" title="Ego Trippin&#39;">Ego Trippin'</a></i>. Priority Records released his album <i><a href="/wiki/Malice_%27n_Wonderland" class="mw-redirect" title="Malice &#39;n Wonderland">Malice 'n Wonderland</a></i> in 2009, followed by <i><a href="/wiki/Doggumentary" title="Doggumentary">Doggumentary</a></i> in 2011. Snoop Dogg has starred in motion pictures and hosted several television shows, including <i><a href="/wiki/Doggy_Fizzle_Televizzle" title="Doggy Fizzle Televizzle">Doggy Fizzle Televizzle</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg%27s_Father_Hood" title="Snoop Dogg&#39;s Father Hood">Snoop Dogg's Father Hood</a>,</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dogg_After_Dark" title="Dogg After Dark">Dogg After Dark</a></i>. He also coaches a youth football league and high-school football team. In September 2009, EMI hired him as the chairman of a reactivated Priority Records.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, after a trip to <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, Broadus announced a conversion to <a href="/wiki/Rastafari" title="Rastafari">Rastafari</a> and a new alias, Snoop Lion. As Snoop Lion he released a <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> album, <i><a href="/wiki/Reincarnated_(album)" title="Reincarnated (album)">Reincarnated</a>,</i> and a <a href="/wiki/Reincarnated_(film)" title="Reincarnated (film)">documentary film of the same name</a>, about his Jamaican experience, in early 2013. His 13th studio album, <a href="/wiki/Bush_(album)" title="Bush (album)"><i>Bush</i></a>, was released in May 2015 and marked a return of the Snoop Dogg name. His 14th solo studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Coolaid" title="Coolaid">Coolaid</a>,</i> was released in July 2016. In March 2016, the night before <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_32" title="WrestleMania 32">WrestleMania 32</a> in <a href="/wiki/Arlington,_Texas" title="Arlington, Texas">Arlington, Texas</a>, he was inducted into the celebrity wing of the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Hall_of_Fame" title="WWE Hall of Fame">WWE Hall of Fame</a>, having made several appearances for the company, including as master of ceremonies during a match at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXIV" title="WrestleMania XXIV">WrestleMania XXIV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, Snoop announced that he was "a <a href="/wiki/Born-again_Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Born-again Christian">born-again Christian</a>" and released his first <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/Bible_of_Love" title="Bible of Love">Bible of Love</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-BAC_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAC-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> On November 19, 2018, Snoop Dogg was given a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-brooklynvegan1_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brooklynvegan1-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 2022, Snoop Dogg acquired Death Row Records from <a href="/wiki/MNRK_Music_Group" title="MNRK Music Group">MNRK Music Group</a> (formerly known as eOne Music), and released his 19th studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/BODR" title="BODR">BODR</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn.com_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Calvin Cordozar Broadus Jr. was born on October 20, 1971, in <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach,_California" title="Long Beach, California">Long Beach, California</a>, to Vernell Varnado and Beverly Tate.<sup id="cite_ref-wargs.com_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wargs.com-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Vernell, who was a <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> veteran, singer, and mail carrier, left the family only three months after his birth, and thus he was named after his stepfather, Calvin Cordozar Broadus Sr. (1948–1984).<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> His father remained largely absent from his life. As a boy, his mother nicknamed him "<a href="/wiki/Snoopy" title="Snoopy">Snoopy</a>" due to his love and likeness of the cartoon character from <i><a href="/wiki/Peanuts" title="Peanuts">Peanuts</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He was the second of his mother's three sons. His mother and stepfather divorced in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-wargs.com_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wargs.com-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> When Broadus was very young, he began singing and playing piano at the Golgotha Trinity Baptist Church. In sixth grade, he began rapping.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_1993_Growl_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_1993_Growl-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> As a child, Broadus sold candy, delivered newspapers, and bagged groceries to help his family make ends meet. He was described as having been a dedicated student and enthusiastic churchgoer, active in choir and football. Broadus said in 1993 that he began engaging in unlawful activities and joining gangs in his teenage years, despite his mother's preventative efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Broadus would frequently rap in school. As he recalled: "When I rapped in the hallways at school I would draw such a big crowd that the principal would think there was a fight going on. It made me begin to realize that I had a gift. I could tell that my raps interested people and that made me interested in myself."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a teenager, Broadus frequently ran into trouble with the law. He was a member of the Rollin' 20s <a href="/wiki/Crips" title="Crips">Crips</a> gang in the <a href="/wiki/Eastside,_Long_Beach,_California" title="Eastside, Long Beach, California">Eastside</a> neighborhood of Long Beach;<sup id="cite_ref-Most_Lovable_Pimp_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Most_Lovable_Pimp-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> although in 1993 he denied the frequent police and media reports by saying that he never joined a gang.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_1993_Growl_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_1993_Growl-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after graduating from high school at <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach_Polytechnic_High_School" title="Long Beach Polytechnic High School">Long Beach Polytechnic High School</a> in 1989, he was arrested for possession of <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a>, and for the next three years, was frequently incarcerated, including at <a href="/wiki/Peter_J._Pitchess_Detention_Center" title="Peter J. Pitchess Detention Center">Wayside Jail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> With his two cousins, <a href="/wiki/Nate_Dogg" title="Nate Dogg">Nate Dogg</a> and Lil' ½ Dead, and friend <a href="/wiki/Warren_G" title="Warren G">Warren G</a>, he recorded homemade tapes; the four called their group <a href="/wiki/213_(group)" title="213 (group)">213</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Area_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Area code">area code</a> of their native Long Beach at that time. One of Snoop's early solo <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap" title="Freestyle rap">freestyles</a> over "<a href="/wiki/Hold_On_(En_Vogue_song)" title="Hold On (En Vogue song)">Hold On</a>" by <a href="/wiki/En_Vogue" title="En Vogue">En Vogue</a> was on a <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a> that fortuitously wound up with <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>; the influential producer was so impressed by the sample that he called Snoop to audition in 1991 for his label <a href="/wiki/Death_Row_Records" title="Death Row Records">Death Row Records</a> (then known as Future Shock). Former <a href="/wiki/N.W.A" title="N.W.A">N.W.A</a> affiliate, American rapper Tracy Lynn Curry better known as <a href="/wiki/The_D.O.C." title="The D.O.C.">The D.O.C.</a>, taught him to structure his lyrics and separate the themes into verses, hooks, and choruses.<sup id="cite_ref-Hip_Hop_Honours_2007_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hip_Hop_Honours_2007-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_career">Music career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="1992.E2.80.931998:_Death_Row.2C_Doggystyle.2C_and_Tha_Doggfather"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1992–1998:_Death_Row,_Doggystyle,_and_Tha_Doggfather">1992–1998: Death Row, <i>Doggystyle,</i> and <i>Tha Doggfather</i></span></h3>
<p>When he began recording, Broadus took the stage name Snoop Doggy Dogg. <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> began working with him, first on the theme song of the 1992 film <i><a href="/wiki/Deep_Cover" title="Deep Cover">Deep Cover</a></i> and then on Dr. Dre's debut solo album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chronic" title="The Chronic">The Chronic</a></i> along with the other members of his former starting group, <a href="/wiki/Tha_Dogg_Pound" title="Tha Dogg Pound">Tha Dogg Pound</a>. This intense exposure played a considerable part in making Snoop Dogg's debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Doggystyle" title="Doggystyle">Doggystyle</a>,</i> the critical and commercial success that it was.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Snoop_dog-02.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Snoop_dog-02.jpg/220px-Snoop_dog-02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Snoop_dog-02.jpg/330px-Snoop_dog-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Snoop_dog-02.jpg/440px-Snoop_dog-02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1360" data-file-height="912" /></a><figcaption>Snoop Dogg in 1998</figcaption></figure>
<p>Fueling the ascendance of <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_hip_hop" title="West Coast hip hop">West Coast</a> <a href="/wiki/G-funk" title="G-funk">G-funk</a> hip hop, the singles "<a href="/wiki/Who_Am_I_(What%27s_My_Name)%3F" class="mw-redirect" title="Who Am I (What&#39;s My Name)?">Who Am I (What's My Name)?</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Gin_and_Juice" title="Gin and Juice">Gin and Juice</a>" reached the top ten most-played songs in the United States, and the album stayed on the Billboard charts for several months.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">Gangsta rap</a> became the center of arguments about censorship and labeling, with Snoop Dogg often used as an example of violent and <a href="/wiki/Misogynistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Misogynistic">misogynistic</a> musicians.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Unlike much of the harder-edged <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangsta rap</a> artists, Snoop Dogg seemed to show his softer side, according to music journalist <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Philips" title="Chuck Philips">Chuck Philips</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> music critic <a href="/wiki/Tour%C3%A9_(journalist)" title="Touré (journalist)">Touré</a> asserted that Snoop had a relatively soft vocal delivery compared to other rappers: "Snoop's vocal style is part of what distinguishes him: where many rappers scream, figuratively and literally, he speaks softly."<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_1993_Growl_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_1993_Growl-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <i>Doggystyle,</i> much like <i>The Chronic,</i> featured a host of rappers signed to or affiliated with the Death Row label including <a href="/wiki/Daz_Dillinger" title="Daz Dillinger">Daz Dillinger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurupt" title="Kurupt">Kurupt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nate_Dogg" title="Nate Dogg">Nate Dogg</a>, and others.
</p><p>In 1993, Broadus was charged with first-degree murder for the shooting of Philip Woldermariam, a member of a rival gang who was actually killed by Snoop's bodyguard, McKinley Lee, aka Malik.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Broadus was acquitted on February 20, 1996. According to Broadus, after he was acquitted he did not want to continue living the "gangsta" lifestyle, because he felt that continuing his behavior would result in his assassination or a prison term.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> A short film about Snoop Dogg's murder trial, <i><a href="/wiki/Murder_Was_the_Case" title="Murder Was the Case">Murder Was the Case</a>,</i> was released in 1994, along with an accompanying <a href="/wiki/Murder_Was_the_Case_(soundtrack)" class="mw-redirect" title="Murder Was the Case (soundtrack)">soundtrack</a>. On July 6, 1995, <a href="/wiki/Doggystyle_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Doggystyle Records">Doggy Style Records, Inc.</a>, a record label founded by Snoop Dogg, was registered with the <a href="/wiki/California_Secretary_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="California Secretary of State">California Secretary of State</a> as business entity number C1923139.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After his acquittal Snoop and the mother of his son along with their kennel of 20 pit bulls moved into a 5,000-square-foot (460&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) home in the hills of <a href="/wiki/Claremont,_California" title="Claremont, California">Claremont, California</a> and by August 1996 <a href="/wiki/Doggy_Style_Records" title="Doggy Style Records">Doggy Style Records</a>, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Death_Row_Records" title="Death Row Records">Death Row Records</a>, signed <a href="/wiki/The_Gap_Band" title="The Gap Band">the Gap Band</a> <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Wilson_(singer)" title="Charlie Wilson (singer)">Charlie Wilson</a> as one of its first artists.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He collaborated with fellow rap artist <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac Shakur</a> on the 1996 single "<a href="/wiki/2_of_Amerikaz_Most_Wanted" title="2 of Amerikaz Most Wanted">2 of Amerikaz Most Wanted</a>". This was one of Shakur's last songs while alive; <a href="/wiki/Murder_of_Tupac_Shakur" title="Murder of Tupac Shakur">he was shot</a> on September 7, 1996, in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>, dying six days later.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Snoop_Dogg_with_Maynard_James_Keenan_of_Tool.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Snoop_Dogg_with_Maynard_James_Keenan_of_Tool.jpg/220px-Snoop_Dogg_with_Maynard_James_Keenan_of_Tool.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="236" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Snoop_Dogg_with_Maynard_James_Keenan_of_Tool.jpg/330px-Snoop_Dogg_with_Maynard_James_Keenan_of_Tool.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Snoop_Dogg_with_Maynard_James_Keenan_of_Tool.jpg/440px-Snoop_Dogg_with_Maynard_James_Keenan_of_Tool.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1218" data-file-height="1307" /></a><figcaption>Snoop Dogg (left) with <a href="/wiki/Maynard_James_Keenan" title="Maynard James Keenan">Maynard James Keenan</a> in 2001</figcaption></figure>
<p>By the time Snoop Dogg's second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Doggfather" title="Tha Doggfather">Tha Doggfather</a>,</i> was released in November 1996, the price of appearing to be a gang member "<i>living the gangsta</i> <i>life</i>" had become very evident. Among the many notable hip hop industry deaths and convictions were the death of Snoop Dogg's friend and labelmate <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac Shakur</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Racket_(crime)" class="mw-redirect" title="Racket (crime)">racketeering</a> indictment of Death Row co-founder <a href="/wiki/Suge_Knight" title="Suge Knight">Suge Knight</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Dr. Dre had left Death Row earlier in 1996 because of a contract dispute, so Snoop Dogg co-produced <i>Tha Doggfather</i> with <a href="/wiki/Daz_Dillinger" title="Daz Dillinger">Daz Dillinger</a> and <a href="/wiki/DJ_Pooh" title="DJ Pooh">DJ Pooh</a>.
</p><p>This album featured a distinct change of style from <i>Doggystyle,</i> and the leadoff single, "<a href="/wiki/Snoop%27s_Upside_Ya_Head" title="Snoop&#39;s Upside Ya Head">Snoop's Upside Ya Head</a>", featured a collaboration with  Charlie Wilson The album sold reasonably well but was not as successful as its predecessor. <i>Tha Doggfather</i> had a somewhat softer approach to the G-funk style. After Dr. Dre withdrew from Death Row Records, Snoop realized that he was subject to an ironclad time-based contract (i.e., that Death Row practically owned anything he produced for a number of years), and refused to produce anymore tracks for <a href="/wiki/Suge_Knight" title="Suge Knight">Suge Knight</a> other than the insulting "Fuck Death Row" until his contract expired.<sup id="cite_ref-Most_Lovable_Pimp_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Most_Lovable_Pimp-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Neil_Strauss" title="Neil Strauss">Neil Strauss</a> in 1998, Snoop Dogg said that though he had been given lavish gifts by his former label, they had withheld his royalty payments.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Stephen Thomas Erlewine of Allmusic said that after <i>Tha Doggfather,</i> Snoop Dogg began "moving away from his gangsta roots toward a calmer lyrical aesthetic":<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> for instance, Snoop participated in the 1997 <a href="/wiki/Lollapalooza" title="Lollapalooza">Lollapalooza</a> concert tour, which featured mainly alternative rock music. Troy J. Augusto of <i>Variety</i> noticed that Snoop's set at Lollapalooza attracted "much dancing, and, strangely, even a small mosh pit" in the audience.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1998.E2.80.932006:_Signing_with_No_Limit_and_continued_success"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1998–2006:_Signing_with_No_Limit_and_continued_success">1998–2006: Signing with No Limit and continued success</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Snoop_Dogg_Hawaii.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Snoop_Dogg_Hawaii.jpg/170px-Snoop_Dogg_Hawaii.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="238" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Snoop_Dogg_Hawaii.jpg/255px-Snoop_Dogg_Hawaii.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Snoop_Dogg_Hawaii.jpg/340px-Snoop_Dogg_Hawaii.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="2100" /></a><figcaption>Snoop Dogg performing in Hawaii for U.S. military members in 2005</figcaption></figure>
<p>Snoop signed with <a href="/wiki/Master_P" title="Master P">Master P</a>'s <a href="/wiki/No_Limit_Records" title="No Limit Records">No Limit Records</a> (distributed by <a href="/wiki/Priority_Records" title="Priority Records">Priority</a>/<a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a> Records) in March 1998 and debuted on the label with <i><a href="/wiki/Da_Game_Is_to_Be_Sold,_Not_to_Be_Told" title="Da Game Is to Be Sold, Not to Be Told">Da Game Is to Be Sold, Not to Be Told</a></i> later that year. He said at the time that "Snoop Dogg is universal so he can fit into any camp-especially a camp that knows how to handmake shit[;] [a]nd, No Limit hand makes material. They make material fittin' to the artist and they know what type of shit Snoop Dogg is supposed to be on. That's why it's so tight." &#32;&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>&#93;<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> His other albums on No Limit were <i><a href="/wiki/No_Limit_Top_Dogg" title="No Limit Top Dogg">No Limit Top Dogg</a></i> in 1999 (selling over 1,510,000 copies) and <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Last_Meal" title="Tha Last Meal">Tha Last Meal</a></i> in 2000 (selling over 2,100,000).<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_12-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1999, his autobiography, <i>Tha Doggfather,</i> was published.
</p><p>In 2002, he released the album <i><a href="/wiki/Paid_tha_Cost_to_Be_da_Boss" title="Paid tha Cost to Be da Boss">Paid tha Cost to Be da Bo$$</a>,</i> on Priority/<a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol</a>/<a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a>, selling over 1,310,000 copies. The album featured the hit singles "<a href="/wiki/From_tha_Chuuuch_to_da_Palace" title="From tha Chuuuch to da Palace">From tha Chuuuch to da Palace</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_(Snoop_Dogg_song)" title="Beautiful (Snoop Dogg song)">Beautiful</a>", featuring guest vocals by <a href="/wiki/Pharrell" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharrell">Pharrell</a>. In the same year, he featured in the remix of <a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_Atlanta" title="Welcome to Atlanta">Welcome to Atlanta</a> by <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Dupri" title="Jermaine Dupri">Jermaine Dupri</a>. By this stage in his career, Snoop Dogg had left behind his "<a href="/wiki/Gangster" title="Gangster">gangster</a>" image and embraced a "<a href="/wiki/Pimp" class="mw-redirect" title="Pimp">pimp</a>" image.
</p><p>In June 2004, Snoop signed to <a href="/wiki/Geffen_Records" title="Geffen Records">Geffen Records</a>/<a href="/wiki/Star_Trak_Entertainment" title="Star Trak Entertainment">Star Trak Entertainment</a>, both distributed by <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>; Star Trak is headed by producer duo <a href="/wiki/The_Neptunes" title="The Neptunes">the Neptunes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> which produced several tracks for Snoop's 2004 release <i><a href="/wiki/R%26G_(Rhythm_%26_Gangsta):_The_Masterpiece" title="R&amp;G (Rhythm &amp; Gangsta): The Masterpiece">R&amp;G (Rhythm &amp; Gangsta): The Masterpiece</a></i>. "<a href="/wiki/Drop_It_Like_It%27s_Hot" title="Drop It Like It&#39;s Hot">Drop It Like It's Hot</a>" (featuring Pharrell), the first single released from the album, was a hit and became Snoop Dogg's first single to reach number one. His third release was "<a href="/wiki/Signs_(Snoop_Dogg_song)" title="Signs (Snoop Dogg song)">Signs</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Wilson_(musician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Charlie Wilson (musician)">Charlie Wilson</a>, which entered the UK chart at No. 2. This was his highest entry ever in the UK chart. The album sold 1,730,000 copies in the U.S. alone, and most of its singles were heavily played on radio and television. Snoop Dogg joined <a href="/wiki/Warren_G" title="Warren G">Warren G</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nate_Dogg" title="Nate Dogg">Nate Dogg</a> to form the group <a href="/wiki/213_(group)" title="213 (group)">213</a> and released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hard_Way_(213_album)" title="The Hard Way (213 album)">The Hard Way</a></i> in 2004. Debuting at No.4 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and No.1 on the Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums, it included the single "Groupie Luv". Snoop Dogg <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">appeared</a> in the music video for <a href="/wiki/Korn" title="Korn">Korn</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Twisted_Transistor" title="Twisted Transistor">Twisted Transistor</a>" along with fellow rappers <a href="/wiki/Lil_Jon" title="Lil Jon">Lil Jon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xzibit" title="Xzibit">Xzibit</a>, and <a href="/wiki/David_Banner" title="David Banner">David Banner</a>.
</p><p>Snoop Dogg appeared on two tracks from Ice Cube's 2006 album <i><a href="/wiki/Laugh_Now,_Cry_Later" title="Laugh Now, Cry Later">Laugh Now, Cry Later</a>,</i> including "<a href="/wiki/Go_to_Church" title="Go to Church">Go to Church</a>", and on several tracks on <a href="/wiki/Tha_Dogg_Pound" title="Tha Dogg Pound">Tha Dogg Pound</a>'s <i>Cali Iz Active</i> the same year. His song "Real Talk" was leaked on the Internet in the summer of 2006 and a video was later released on the Internet. "Real Talk" was dedicated to former Crips leader <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Williams" title="Stanley Williams">Stanley "Tookie" Williams</a> and a diss to <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a>, the governor of California. Two other singles on which Snoop made a guest performance were "Keep Bouncing" by <a href="/wiki/Too_$hort" class="mw-redirect" title="Too $hort">Too $hort</a> (also with <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas" class="mw-redirect" title="The Black Eyed Peas">the Black Eyed Peas</a>) and "<a href="/wiki/Gangsta_Walk" title="Gangsta Walk">Gangsta Walk</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Coolio" title="Coolio">Coolio</a>.
</p><p>Snoop's 2006 album <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Blue_Carpet_Treatment" title="Tha Blue Carpet Treatment">Tha Blue Carpet Treatment</a></i> debuted on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> at No.5 and sold over 850,000 copies. The album and the second single "<a href="/wiki/That%27s_That_Shit" class="mw-redirect" title="That&#39;s That Shit">That's That Shit</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/R._Kelly" title="R. Kelly">R. Kelly</a> were well received by critics. In the album, he collaborated in a video with <a href="/wiki/E-40" title="E-40">E-40</a> and other West Coast rappers on the single "<a href="/wiki/Candy_(Drippin%27_Like_Water)" title="Candy (Drippin&#39; Like Water)">Candy (Drippin' Like Water)</a>".
</p>
<h3><span id="2007.E2.80.932012:_Ego_Trippin.27.2C_Malice_n_Wonderland_and_Doggumentary"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2007–2012:_Ego_Trippin',_Malice_n_Wonderland_and_Doggumentary">2007–2012: <i>Ego Trippin',</i> <i>Malice n Wonderland</i> and <i>Doggumentary</i></span></h3>
<p>In July 2007, Snoop Dogg made history by becoming the first artist to release a track as a <a href="/wiki/Ringtone" title="Ringtone">ringtone</a> before its release as a single, "It's the D.O.G." On July 7, 2007, Snoop Dogg performed at the <a href="/wiki/Live_Earth_concert,_Hamburg" title="Live Earth concert, Hamburg">Live Earth concert, Hamburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Snoop Dogg has ventured into singing for <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" class="mw-redirect" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> with his first ever rap for an <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_India" title="Cinema of India">Indian movie</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Singh_Is_Kinng" title="Singh Is Kinng">Singh Is Kinng</a></i>; the song title is also "Singh is Kinng". He appears in the movie as himself.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The album featuring the song was released on June 8, 2008, on Junglee Music Records.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> He released his ninth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Ego_Trippin%27" title="Ego Trippin&#39;">Ego Trippin'</a></i> (selling 400,000 copies in the U.S.), along with the first single, "<a href="/wiki/Sexual_Eruption" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual Eruption">Sexual Eruption</a>". The single peaked at No. 7 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_100" class="mw-redirect" title="Billboard 100"><i>Billboard</i> 100</a>, featuring Snoop using <a href="/wiki/Autotune" class="mw-redirect" title="Autotune">autotune</a>. The album featured production from <a href="/wiki/QDT" title="QDT">QDT</a> (Quik-Dogg-Teddy).
</p><p>Snoop was appointed an executive position at Priority Records. His tenth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Malice_n_Wonderland" title="Malice n Wonderland">Malice n Wonderland</a>,</i> was released on December 8, 2009. The first single from the album, "<a href="/wiki/Gangsta_Luv" title="Gangsta Luv">Gangsta Luv</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a>, peaked at No.35 on the Billboard Hot 100. The album debuted at No.23 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, selling 61,000 copies its first week, making it his lowest charting album. His third single, "<a href="/wiki/I_Wanna_Rock_(Snoop_Dogg_song)" title="I Wanna Rock (Snoop Dogg song)">I Wanna Rock</a>", peaked at No.41 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. The fourth single from <i>Malice n Wonderland,</i> titled "Pronto", featuring <a href="/wiki/Soulja_Boy_Tell_%27Em" class="mw-redirect" title="Soulja Boy Tell &#39;Em">Soulja Boy Tell 'Em</a>, was released on <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> on December 1, 2009. Snoop re-released the album under the name <i>More Malice</i>.
</p><p>Snoop collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a> on "<a href="/wiki/California_Gurls" title="California Gurls">California Gurls</a>", the first single from her album <i><a href="/wiki/Teenage_Dream_(Katy_Perry_album)" title="Teenage Dream (Katy Perry album)">Teenage Dream</a>,</i> which was released on May 7, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-FMQB_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FMQB-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Snoop can also be heard on the track "Flashing" by Dr. Dre and on <a href="/wiki/Currensy" title="Currensy">Curren$y</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Seat_Change_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Seat Change (song)">Seat Change</a>". He was also featured on a new single from Australian singer <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Mauboy" title="Jessica Mauboy">Jessica Mauboy</a>, titled "<a href="/wiki/Get_%27em_Girls_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Get &#39;em Girls (song)">Get 'em Girls</a>" (released September 2010). Snoop's latest effort was backing American recording artist, <a href="/wiki/Emii" title="Emii">Emii</a>, on her second single entitled "Mr. Romeo" (released October 26, 2010, as a follow-up to "Magic"). Snoop also collaborated with American comedy troupe <a href="/wiki/The_Lonely_Island" title="The Lonely Island">the Lonely Island</a> in their song "Turtleneck &amp; Chain", in their 2011 album <i><a href="/wiki/Turtleneck_%26_Chain" title="Turtleneck &amp; Chain">Turtleneck &amp; Chain</a></i>.
</p><p>Snoop Dogg's eleventh studio album is <i><a href="/wiki/Doggumentary" title="Doggumentary">Doggumentary</a></i>. The album went through several tentative titles including <i>Doggystyle 2: Tha Doggumentary</i> and <i>Doggumentary Music: 0020</i> before being released under the final title <i>Doggumentary</i> during March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Snoop was featured on <a href="/wiki/Gorillaz" title="Gorillaz">Gorillaz</a>' album <i><a href="/wiki/Plastic_Beach" title="Plastic Beach">Plastic Beach</a></i> on a track called: "Welcome to the World of the Plastic Beach" with the <a href="/wiki/Hypnotic_Brass_Ensemble" title="Hypnotic Brass Ensemble">Hypnotic Brass Ensemble</a>, he also completed another track with them entitled "Sumthing Like This Night" which does not appear on <i>Plastic Beach,</i> yet does appear on <i>Doggumentary</i>. He also appears on the latest <a href="/wiki/Tech_N9ne" title="Tech N9ne">Tech N9ne</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/All_6%27s_and_7%27s" title="All 6&#39;s and 7&#39;s">All 6's and 7's</a></i> (released June 7, 2011) on a track called "Pornographic" which also features <a href="/wiki/E-40" title="E-40">E-40</a> and <a href="/wiki/Krizz_Kaliko" title="Krizz Kaliko">Krizz Kaliko</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.932013:_Reincarnated_and_7_Days_of_Funk"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–2013:_Reincarnated_and_7_Days_of_Funk">2012–2013: <i>Reincarnated</i> and <i>7 Days of Funk</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Snoop_Dogg_snapped_attending_a_press_conference_in_India.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Snoop_Dogg_snapped_attending_a_press_conference_in_India.jpg/170px-Snoop_Dogg_snapped_attending_a_press_conference_in_India.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="235" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Snoop_Dogg_snapped_attending_a_press_conference_in_India.jpg/255px-Snoop_Dogg_snapped_attending_a_press_conference_in_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Snoop_Dogg_snapped_attending_a_press_conference_in_India.jpg/340px-Snoop_Dogg_snapped_attending_a_press_conference_in_India.jpg 2x" data-file-width="501" data-file-height="692" /></a><figcaption>Snoop Dogg as Snoop Lion, 2013</figcaption></figure>
<p>On February 4, 2012, Snoop Dogg announced a documentary, <i><a href="/wiki/Reincarnated_(film)" title="Reincarnated (film)">Reincarnated</a>,</i> alongside his new upcoming studio album entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Reincarnated_(album)" title="Reincarnated (album)">Reincarnated</a></i>. The film was released March 21, 2013, with the album slated for release April 23, 2013. On July 20, 2012, Snoop Dogg released a new <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> single, "La La La" under the pseudonym Snoop Lion.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Three other songs were also announced to be on the album: "No Guns Allowed", "Ashtrays and Heartbreaks", and "Harder Times".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 31, 2012, Snoop introduced a new stage name, Snoop Lion. He told reporters that he was rechristened Snoop Lion by a <a href="/wiki/Rastafari" title="Rastafari">Rastafari</a> priest in <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In response to <a href="/wiki/Frank_Ocean" title="Frank Ocean">Frank Ocean</a> coming out, Snoop said hip hop was ready to accept a gay rapper.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Snoop recorded an original song for the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Fighting_game" title="Fighting game">fighting game</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Tekken_Tag_Tournament_2" title="Tekken Tag Tournament 2">Tekken Tag Tournament 2</a>,</i> titled "Knocc 'Em Down"; and makes a special appearance as a non-playable character in "The Snoop Dogg Stage" arena.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September of the same year, Snoop released a compilation of electronic music entitled <i>Loose Joints</i> under the moniker DJ Snoopadelic, stating the influence of <a href="/wiki/George_Clinton_(funk_musician)" title="George Clinton (funk musician)">George Clinton</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Funkadelic" title="Funkadelic">Funkadelic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fader_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fader-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fader" title="The Fader">The Fader</a></i> magazine, Snoop stated "Snoop Lion, Snoop Dogg, DJ Snoopadelic—they only know one thing: make music that's timeless and bangs."<sup id="cite_ref-Fader_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fader-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In December 2012, Snoop released his second single from <i>Reincarnated,</i> "Here Comes the King". It was also announced that Snoop worked a deal with RCA Records to release <i>Reincarnated</i> in early 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Also in December 2012, Snoop Dogg released a <i>That's My Work</i> a collaboration rap mixtape with Tha Dogg Pound.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Benzino" title="Benzino">Hip Hop Weekly</a></i> on June 17, producer <a href="/wiki/Symbolyc_One_(S1)" class="mw-redirect" title="Symbolyc One (S1)">Symbolyc One (S1)</a> announced that Snoop was working on his final album under his rap moniker Snoop Dogg; "I've been working with Snoop, he's actually working on his last solo album as Snoop Dogg."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In September 2013, Snoop released a collaboration album with his sons as Tha Broadus Boyz titled <i>Royal Fam</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx.com_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx.com-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> On October 28, 2013, Snoop Dogg released another mixtape entitled <i>That's My Work 2</i> hosted by <a href="/wiki/DJ_Drama" title="DJ Drama">DJ Drama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Snoop formed a funk duo with musician <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A2m-Funk" title="Dâm-Funk">Dâm-Funk</a> called 7 Days of Funk and released their <a href="/wiki/7_Days_of_Funk" class="mw-redirect" title="7 Days of Funk">eponymous debut album</a> on December 10, 2013.
</p>
<h3><span id="2014.E2.80.932017:_Bush.2C_Coolaid.2C_and_Neva_Left"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–2017:_Bush,_Coolaid,_and_Neva_Left">2014–2017: <i>Bush,</i> <i>Coolaid,</i> and <i>Neva Left</i></span></h3>
<p>In August 2014, a clip surfaced online featuring a sneak preview of a song Snoop had recorded for Pharrell.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Snoop's <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a>-produced album <i><a href="/wiki/Bush_(album)" title="Bush (album)">Bush</a></i> was released on May 12, 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> with the first single "<a href="/wiki/Peaches_N_Cream_(Snoop_Dogg_song)" title="Peaches N Cream (Snoop Dogg song)">Peaches N Cream</a>" having been released on March 10, 2015.
</p><p>On June 13, 2016, Snoop Dogg announced the release date for his album <i><a href="/wiki/Coolaid" title="Coolaid">Coolaid</a>,</i> which was released on July 1, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> He headlined a "unity party" for donors at Philly's Electric Factory on July 28, 2016, the last day of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_National_Convention" title="Democratic National Convention">Democratic National Convention</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Released March 1, 2017, through his own Doggy Style Records, "Promise You This" precedes the release of his upcoming <i>Coolaid</i> film based on the album of the same name. Snoop Dogg released his fifteenth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Neva_Left" title="Neva Left">Neva Left</a></i> in May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2018.E2.80.932021:_Bible_of_Love.2C_I_Wanna_Thank_Me.2C_and_From_tha_Streets_2_tha_Suites"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–2021:_Bible_of_Love,_I_Wanna_Thank_Me,_and_From_tha_Streets_2_tha_Suites">2018–2021: <i>Bible of Love</i>, <i>I Wanna Thank Me</i>, and <i>From tha Streets 2 tha Suites</i></span></h3><p>
He released a gospel album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Bible_of_Love" title="Bible of Love">Bible of Love</a></i> on March 16, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> </p><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Jamiroquai_2018_Coachella18W1-147_(41157702225).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Jamiroquai_2018_Coachella18W1-147_%2841157702225%29.jpg/220px-Jamiroquai_2018_Coachella18W1-147_%2841157702225%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Jamiroquai_2018_Coachella18W1-147_%2841157702225%29.jpg/330px-Jamiroquai_2018_Coachella18W1-147_%2841157702225%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Jamiroquai_2018_Coachella18W1-147_%2841157702225%29.jpg/440px-Jamiroquai_2018_Coachella18W1-147_%2841157702225%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5204" data-file-height="2921" /></a><figcaption>Snoop performing with <a href="/wiki/Jamiroquai" title="Jamiroquai">Jamiroquai</a> at <a href="/wiki/Coachella_(festival)" title="Coachella (festival)">Coachella</a>)</figcaption></figure><p> In April 2018, Snoop performed at <a href="/wiki/Coachella_(festival)" title="Coachella (festival)">Coachella</a> with acid-jazz and funk band <a href="/wiki/Jamiroquai" title="Jamiroquai">Jamiroquai</a>. Snoop was featured on <a href="/wiki/Gorillaz" title="Gorillaz">Gorillaz</a>' album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Now_Now" title="The Now Now">The Now Now</a></i>, released in June 2018, on a track called: "Hollywood" with <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Principle" title="Jamie Principle">Jamie Principle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In November 2018, Snoop Dogg announced plans for his Puff Puff Pass tour, which features Bone Thugs-n-Harmony, <a href="/wiki/Too_Short" title="Too Short">Too $hort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warren_G" title="Warren G">Warren G</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurupt" title="Kurupt">Kurupt</a>, and others. The tour ran from November 24 to January 5.<sup id="cite_ref-brooklynvegan1_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brooklynvegan1-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Snoop Dogg was featured on <a href="/wiki/Lil_Dicky" title="Lil Dicky">Lil Dicky</a>'s April 2019 single "<a href="/wiki/Earth_(Lil_Dicky_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Earth (Lil Dicky song)">Earth</a>", where he played the role of a <a href="/wiki/Cannabis" title="Cannabis">marijuana plant</a> in both the song's lyrics and animated video.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On July 3, 2019, Snoop Dogg released the title track from his upcoming 17th studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/I_Wanna_Thank_Me" title="I Wanna Thank Me">I Wanna Thank Me</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The album was released on August 16, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Snoop Dogg collaborated with Vietnamese singer <a href="/wiki/Son_Tung_M-TP" class="mw-redirect" title="Son Tung M-TP">Son Tung M-TP</a> in "Hãy trao cho anh" ("Give it to Me"), which was officially released on July 1, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> As of October 3, 2019, the music video has amassed over 158 million views on YouTube.
</p><p>Early in 2020, it was announced that Snoop had rescheduled his tour in support of his <i>I Wanna Thank You</i> album and documentary of the same name. The tour has been rescheduled to commence in February 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In May 2020, Snoop released the song "Que Maldicion", a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Banda_MS" title="Banda MS">Banda Sinaloense de Sergio Lizarraga</a>, peaking at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_Hot_100" title="Bubbling Under Hot 100">Bubbling Under Hot 100</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 20, 2021, Snoop Dogg released his eighteenth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/From_tha_Streets_2_tha_Suites" title="From tha Streets 2 tha Suites">From tha Streets 2 tha Suites</a></i>. It was announced on April 7, 2021, via <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The album received generally positive reviews from critics.
</p><p>During an interview on the September 27 airing of <i>The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon</i>, Snoop Dogg announced <i><a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg_Presents_Algorithm" title="Snoop Dogg Presents Algorithm">Algorithm</a></i>. The album was released on November 19, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2022:_Super_Bowl_LVI_halftime_show_performance.2C_BODR_and_Missionary"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2022:_Super_Bowl_LVI_halftime_show_performance,_BODR_and_Missionary">2022: Super Bowl LVI halftime show performance, <i>BODR</i> and <i>Missionary</i></span></h3>
<p>Snoop Dogg performed at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVI_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl LVI halftime show">halftime show</a> of <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVI" title="Super Bowl LVI">Super Bowl LVI</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2022, Snoop Dogg announced that he would release his 19th studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/BODR" title="BODR">BODR</a></i>, on the same day as his Super Bowl Halftime Show performance.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> However, the album's release was pushed forward two days and was released on February 11, 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 10, 2022, Snoop Dogg announced that he has acquired Death Row Records and intends to revive the label.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 24, 2022, Snoop Dogg collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> on the track "<a href="/wiki/From_the_D_2_the_LBC" title="From the D 2 the LBC">From the D 2 the LBC</a>", with a live-action/animated music video released the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later that year, Snoop Dogg has revealed he has a new album coming out called <i>Missionary</i> and it's entirely produced by Dr. Dre. The album will be released via Death Row/Aftermath.<sup id="cite_ref-complex.com_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex.com-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span></h2>
<p>Broadus has appeared in numerous films and television episodes throughout his career. His starring roles in film includes <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wash_(2001_film)" title="The Wash (2001 film)">The Wash</a></i> (with Dr. Dre) and the horror film <i><a href="/wiki/Bones_(2001_film)" title="Bones (2001 film)">Bones</a></i>. He also co-starred with rapper Wiz Khalifa in the 2012 movie <i><a href="/wiki/Mac_and_Devin_Go_to_High_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Mac and Devin Go to High School">Mac and Devin Go to High School</a></i> which a sequel has been announced.<sup id="cite_ref-rapradar1_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rapradar1-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> He has had various supporting and cameo roles in film, including <i><a href="/wiki/Half_Baked" title="Half Baked">Half Baked</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Training_Day" title="Training Day">Training Day</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Starsky_%26_Hutch_(film)" title="Starsky &amp; Hutch (film)">Starsky &amp; Hutch</a>,</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BCno" title="Brüno">Brüno</a></i>.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:BunnyMania.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/BunnyMania.jpg/220px-BunnyMania.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/BunnyMania.jpg/330px-BunnyMania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/BunnyMania.jpg/440px-BunnyMania.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="370" /></a><figcaption>Snoop Dogg at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXIV" title="WrestleMania XXIV">WrestleMania XXIV</a> at Orlando's <a href="/wiki/Citrus_Bowl_(stadium)" class="mw-redirect" title="Citrus Bowl (stadium)">Citrus Bowl</a> with <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Massaro" title="Ashley Massaro">Ashley Massaro</a> and tag team partner <a href="/wiki/Maria_Kanellis" title="Maria Kanellis">Maria</a>, March 30, 2008</figcaption></figure>
<p>He has starred in three television programs: sketch-comedy show <i><a href="/wiki/Doggy_Fizzle_Televizzle" title="Doggy Fizzle Televizzle">Doggy Fizzle Televizzle</a>,</i><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> variety show <i><a href="/wiki/Dogg_After_Dark" title="Dogg After Dark">Dogg After Dark</a>,</i><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and reality show <i><a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg%27s_Father_Hood" title="Snoop Dogg&#39;s Father Hood">Snoop Dogg's Father Hood</a></i> (also starring Snoop's wife and children).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> He has starred in episodes of <i><a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Hill" title="King of the Hill">King of the Hill</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_(TV_series)" title="Las Vegas (TV series)">Las Vegas</a>,</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Monk_(TV_series)" title="Monk (TV series)">Monk</a>,</i> one episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Robot_Chicken" title="Robot Chicken">Robot Chicken</a>,</i><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> as well as three episodes of <i><a href="/wiki/One_Life_to_Live" title="One Life to Live">One Life to Live</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> He has participated in three <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central_Roast" title="Comedy Central Roast">Comedy Central Roasts</a>, for <a href="/wiki/Flavor_Flav" title="Flavor Flav">Flavor Flav</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a>. Cameo television appearances include episodes of <i><a href="/wiki/The_L_Word" title="The L Word">The L Word</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Weeds_(TV_series)" title="Weeds (TV series)">Weeds</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Entourage_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Entourage (U.S. TV series)">Entourage</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/I_Get_That_a_Lot" title="I Get That a Lot">I Get That a Lot</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Monk_(TV_Series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Monk (TV Series)">Monk</a>,</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Price_Is_Right_(U.S._game_show)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Price Is Right (U.S. game show)">The Price Is Right</a></i>. He has also appeared in an episode of the YouTube video series, <i><a href="/wiki/Epic_Rap_Battles_of_History" title="Epic Rap Battles of History">Epic Rap Battles of History</a></i> as <a href="/wiki/Moses" title="Moses">Moses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2000, Broadus (as "Michael J. Corleone") directed <i><a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg%27s_Doggystyle" title="Snoop Dogg&#39;s Doggystyle">Snoop Dogg's Doggystyle</a>,</i> a <a href="/wiki/Pornographic_film" title="Pornographic film">pornographic film</a> produced by <a href="/wiki/Hustler_(magazine)" title="Hustler (magazine)">Hustler</a>. The film, combining hip hop with x-rated material, was a huge success and won "Top Selling Release of the Year" at the 2002 <a href="/wiki/AVN_Awards" title="AVN Awards">AVN Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Snoop then directed <i><a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg%27s_Hustlaz:_Diary_of_a_Pimp" title="Snoop Dogg&#39;s Hustlaz: Diary of a Pimp">Snoop Dogg's Hustlaz: Diary of a Pimp</a></i> in 2002 (using the nickname "Snoop Scorsese").<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Broadus founded his own production company, <a href="/wiki/Snoopadelic_Films" title="Snoopadelic Films">Snoopadelic Films</a>, in 2005. Their debut film was <i><a href="/wiki/Boss%27n_Up" title="Boss&#39;n Up">Boss'n Up</a>,</i> a film inspired by Snoop Dogg's album <i>R&amp;G,</i> starring <a href="/wiki/Lil_Jon" title="Lil Jon">Lil Jon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trina" title="Trina">Trina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2013, Broadus performed at the annual <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">Kennedy Center Honors</a> concert, honoring jazz pianist <a href="/wiki/Herbie_Hancock" title="Herbie Hancock">Herbie Hancock</a>. After his performance, Snoop credited Hancock with "inventing hip-hop".<sup id="cite_ref-Kennedy_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kennedy-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On several occasions, Broadus has appeared at the <a href="/wiki/Players_Ball" title="Players Ball">Players Ball</a> in support of <a href="/wiki/Don_%22Magic%22_Juan" title="Don &quot;Magic&quot; Juan">Bishop Don Magic Juan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Juan appeared on Snoop's videos for "Boss Playa", "A.D.I.D.A.C.", "P.I.M.P. (Remix)", "Nuthin' Without Me" and "A Pimp's Christmas Song".
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Snoop_Dogg_(20985801623).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Snoop_Dogg_%2820985801623%29.jpg/220px-Snoop_Dogg_%2820985801623%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Snoop_Dogg_%2820985801623%29.jpg/330px-Snoop_Dogg_%2820985801623%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Snoop_Dogg_%2820985801623%29.jpg/440px-Snoop_Dogg_%2820985801623%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832" /></a><figcaption>Snoop Dogg speaks onstage during day one of TechCrunch Disrupt SF 2015.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In January 2016, a Change.org petition was created in the hopes of having Broadus narrate the entire <i><a href="/wiki/Planet_Earth_(2006_TV_series)" title="Planet Earth (2006 TV series)">Planet Earth</a></i> series. The petition comes after Snoop narrated a number of nature clips on <i><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel_Live!" title="Jimmy Kimmel Live!">Jimmy Kimmel Live</a></i><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel_Live!" title="Jimmy Kimmel Live!">!</a><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2016, Broadus performed "Straight outta Compton" and "Fuck tha Police" at <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella</a>, during a reunion of N.W.A. members Dr. Dre, Ice Cube, and MC Ren.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He hosted a Basketball fundraiser "Hoops 4 Water" for <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">Flint, Michigan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Game_Event_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Game_Event-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The event occurred on May 21, 2016, and was run by former Toronto Raptors star and Flint native <a href="/wiki/Morris_Peterson" title="Morris Peterson">Morris Peterson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Game_Event_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Game_Event-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the fall of 2016, VH1 premiered a new show featuring Broadus and his friend <a href="/wiki/Martha_Stewart" title="Martha Stewart">Martha Stewart</a> at called <i><a href="/wiki/Martha_%26_Snoop%27s_Potluck_Dinner_Party" title="Martha &amp; Snoop&#39;s Potluck Dinner Party">Martha &amp; Snoop's Potluck Dinner Party</a>,</i> featuring games, recipes, and musical guests.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Broadus and Stewart also later starred together in a <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_commercials" title="Super Bowl commercials">Super Bowl commercial</a> for <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_US" title="T-Mobile US">T-Mobile</a> during <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LI" title="Super Bowl LI">Super Bowl LI</a> in February 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> With Stewart, Broadus also created a fried chicken recipe, with barbecue flavor potato chips as an added ingredient in the batter.<sup id="cite_ref-SBS_Food_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBS_Food-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017 Broadus hosted a revival of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Joker%27s_Wild" title="The Joker&#39;s Wild">The Joker's Wild</a>,</i> which spent its first two seasons on <a href="/wiki/TBS_(U.S._TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="TBS (U.S. TV channel)">TBS</a> before moving to <a href="/wiki/TNT_(U.S._TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="TNT (U.S. TV network)">TNT</a> in January 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> He is in the film, <i><a href="/wiki/Sponge_on_the_Run" class="mw-redirect" title="Sponge on the Run">Sponge on the Run</a></i>.
</p><p>In October 2018, Broadus released a cookbook, <i>From Crook to Cook: Platinum Recipes from Tha Boss Dogg's Kitchen</i>, containing "50 recipes inspired by Snoop's family staples and favorite comfort foods, with instructions to make everything from fried bologna sandwiches and baked mac and cheese, to soft tacos and orange chicken."<sup id="cite_ref-:1_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The book is coauthored with Ryan Ford and has a foreword by Martha Stewart.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The cookbook had a wave of over 200,000 sales in 2020 and entered the Amazon bestseller list in 2022 after Snoop Dogg's Super Bowl and Puppy Bowl appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early 2020, Broadus launched his debut wine release, under the name "Snoop Cali Red", in a partnership with the Australian wine brand, 19 Crimes. The red wine blend features Snoop's face on the label.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Broadus provided commentary for <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tyson_vs._Roy_Jones_Jr." title="Mike Tyson vs. Roy Jones Jr.">Mike Tyson vs. Roy Jones Jr.</a>, who some pundits described as having "won" the night through his colorful commentary and reactions.<sup id="cite_ref-THR_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THR-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> At one point, Snoop described Tyson and Jones as "like two of my uncles fighting at the barbecue"; he also began singing a <a href="/wiki/Hymn" title="Hymn">hymn</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Take_My_Hand,_Precious_Lord" title="Take My Hand, Precious Lord">Take My Hand, Precious Lord</a>", during the undercard fight between <a href="/wiki/Jake_Paul" title="Jake Paul">Jake Paul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nate_Robinson" title="Nate Robinson">Nate Robinson</a>, after Robinson was knocked down.<sup id="cite_ref-THR_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THR-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2021, Broadus officially joined Def Jam Recordings as its new Executive Creative and Strategic Consultant, a role allowing him to strategically work across the label's executive team and artist roster. His immediate focus was A&amp;R and creative development, reporting to Universal Music Group Chairman &amp; CEO <a href="/wiki/Lucian_Grainge" title="Lucian Grainge">Sir Lucian Grainge</a> as well as Def Jam interim Chairman and CEO Jeffrey Harleston.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> On November 12, 2021, Snoop Dogg announced the signing of <a href="/wiki/Benny_the_Butcher" title="Benny the Butcher">Benny the Butcher</a> on <a href="/wiki/Joe_Rogan" title="Joe Rogan">Joe Rogan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Joe_Rogan_Experience" title="The Joe Rogan Experience">podcast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2022, it was announced that Broadus had fully acquired Death Row Records from its previous owners, <a href="/wiki/EOne_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="EOne Music">The MNRK Music Group</a> (formerly eOne Music). The label was also revived when Snoop Dogg released his 20th album <a href="/wiki/BODR" title="BODR">BODR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 14, 2022, Broadus was added to <a href="/wiki/Call_of_Duty:_Vanguard" title="Call of Duty: Vanguard">Call of Duty: Vanguard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Call_of_Duty:_Warzone" title="Call of Duty: Warzone">Call of Duty: Warzone</a> as an operator as part of the Tracer Pack: Snoop Dogg Operator Bundle available from the in game store.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2022, Broadus was a stakeholder in Fluf World, an <a href="/wiki/NFT" class="mw-redirect" title="NFT">NFT</a> community based on <a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics" title="3D computer graphics">3D</a> rabbit <a href="/wiki/Avatar_(computing)" title="Avatar (computing)">avatars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sloane_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sloane-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_wrestling">Professional wrestling</span></h3>
<p>Snoop Dogg is a lifelong fan of professional wrestling.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> On March 30, 2008, Snoop Dogg appeared at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXIV" title="WrestleMania XXIV">WrestleMania XXIV</a> as a <i>Master of Ceremonies</i> for a tag team match between <a href="/wiki/Maria_Kanellis" title="Maria Kanellis">Maria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Massaro" title="Ashley Massaro">Ashley Massaro</a> as they took on <a href="/wiki/Beth_Phoenix" title="Beth Phoenix">Beth Phoenix</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melina_Perez" title="Melina Perez">Melina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>  On a March 23, 2015, episode of Raw, Snoop Dogg appeared in a segment with <a href="/wiki/Hulk_Hogan" title="Hulk Hogan">Hulk Hogan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Axel" title="Curtis Axel">Curtis Axel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_32" title="WrestleMania 32">WrestleMania 32</a>, he accompanied his cousin <a href="/wiki/Sasha_Banks" title="Sasha Banks">Sasha Banks</a> to the ring for her match, rapping over her theme music. He was also inducted into the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Hall_of_Fame#Class_of_2016" title="WWE Hall of Fame">WWE Hall of Fame</a> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Broadus made a special guest appearance in <a href="/wiki/All_Elite_Wrestling" title="All Elite Wrestling">All Elite Wrestling</a> on the January 6, 2021, episode of <i><a href="/wiki/AEW_Dynamite" title="AEW Dynamite">AEW Dynamite</a></i>, titled <a href="/wiki/AEW_New_Year%27s_Smash" title="AEW New Year&#39;s Smash">New Year's Smash</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> During this appearance, Snoop appeared in the corner of <a href="/wiki/Cody_Rhodes" title="Cody Rhodes">Cody Rhodes</a> during Rhodes's match with <a href="/wiki/Matt_Sydal" title="Matt Sydal">Matt Sydal</a>. He later gave <a href="/wiki/Serpentico" title="Serpentico">Serpentico</a> a <a href="/wiki/Frog_Splash" class="mw-redirect" title="Frog Splash">Frog Splash</a>, with Rhodes then delivering a three-count.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Snoop Dogg would join <a href="/wiki/The_Miz" title="The Miz">The Miz</a> to host both nights of WrestleMania 39. During Night 1, he accompanied <a href="/wiki/Rey_Mysterio" title="Rey Mysterio">Rey Mysterio</a> in a lowrider during his entrance, paying tribute to the late <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Guerrero" title="Eddie Guerrero">Eddie Guerrero</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> On Night 2, he introduced <a href="/wiki/Shane_McMahon" title="Shane McMahon">Shane McMahon</a> to face The Miz in another spontaneous match. McMahon would sustain a quad injury during the match prompting Snoop Dogg to improvise and finish the match himself, ultimately defeating Miz.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Snoop Dogg's improvisational acts were lauded by wrestlers and executives, including WWE chief content officer Triple H.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_ventures_and_investments">Business ventures and investments</span></h3>
<p>Broadus has been an active entrepreneur and investor. In 2009, he was appointed creative chairman of Priority Records.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2013, Broadus and his brand manager Nick Adler released an app, Snoopify, that lets users plaster stickers of Snoop's face, joints or a walrus hat on photos. Adler built the app in May after discovering stickers in Japan. As of 2015, the app was generating $30,000 in weekly sales.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2014, Reddit raised $50 million in a funding round led by <a href="/wiki/Sam_Altman" title="Sam Altman">Sam Altman</a> and including investors <a href="/wiki/Marc_Andreessen" title="Marc Andreessen">Marc Andreessen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Thiel" title="Peter Thiel">Peter Thiel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Conway" title="Ron Conway">Ron Conway</a>, Snoop Dogg, and <a href="/wiki/Jared_Leto" title="Jared Leto">Jared Leto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2015, Broadus became a minority investor in his first investment venture Eaze, a California-based weed delivery startup that promises to deliver medical marijuana to persons' doorsteps in less than 10 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2015, Broadus launched his new digital media business, Merry Jane, that focuses on news about <a href="/wiki/Marijuana_(word)" title="Marijuana (word)">marijuana</a>. "Merry Jane is cannabis 2.0", he said in a promotional video for the media source. "A crossroads of pot culture, business, politics, health."<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2015, Broadus announced his new brand of <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis products</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leafs_By_Snoop" title="Leafs By Snoop">Leafs By Snoop</a>. The line of branded products includes marijuana flowers, concentrates and edibles. "Leafs By Snoop is truly the first mainstream cannabis brand in the world and proud to be a pioneer", he said. In such a way, Broadus became the first major celebrity to brand and market a line of legal marijuana products.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 30, 2016, Broadus was reported to be considering purchasing the famed <a href="/wiki/Soul_food" title="Soul food">soul food</a> restaurant chain <a href="/wiki/Roscoe%27s_House_of_Chicken_and_Waffles" class="mw-redirect" title="Roscoe&#39;s House of Chicken and Waffles">Roscoe's House of Chicken and Waffles</a> out of bankruptcy.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, Broadus ventured into the video game business, creating his own <a href="/wiki/Esports" title="Esports">esports</a> league known as the "Gangsta Gaming League".<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 7, 2022, it was announced that Broadus had joined <a href="/wiki/FaZe_Clan" title="FaZe Clan">FaZe Clan</a> and would be a member of their Board of Directors.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> He would resign from the board of directors in March of the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-fazeres_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fazeres-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 19, 2022, Snoop Dogg ran a poll asking if he should "run twitter". Out of 2.3 million users, 81% said yes.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NFTs">NFTs</span></h3>
<p>On September 21, 2021, Snoop Dogg claimed on Twitter to be a prolific NFT collector known under the pseudonym Cozomo De' Medici.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> In a Vice report following the 2021 claim, reporters Jordan Pearson and Jason Koebler provided evidence disputing the claim that Snoop Dogg and Cozmo De' Medici were the same person.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In a February 2023 interview with Christie's, Medici described the identity reveal as "trolling" and a "stunt".<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<p>Snoop Dogg had been mainly described as a <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-AMG_Doggy_Style_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMG_Doggy_Style-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_hip_hop" title="West Coast hip hop">West Coast hip hop</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-AMG_Doggy_Style_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMG_Doggy_Style-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/G-funk" title="G-funk">g-funk</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_12-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangsta rap</a> artist.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_12-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kool_Moe_Dee" title="Kool Moe Dee">Kool Moe Dee</a> ranks Broadus at No. 33 in his book <i><a href="/wiki/There%27s_a_God_on_the_Mic" title="There&#39;s a God on the Mic">There's a God on the Mic</a>,</i> and says he has "an ultra-smooth, laidback delivery"<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> and "flavor-filled melodic rhyming".<sup id="cite_ref-Kool_Moe_Dee_2003,_p.106_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kool_Moe_Dee_2003,_p.106-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
