</p><p><a href="/wiki/Peter_Shapiro_(journalist)" title="Peter Shapiro (journalist)">Peter Shapiro</a> describes Broadus's delivery as a "<a href="/wiki/Molasses" title="Molasses">molasses</a> <a href="/wiki/Drawl" title="Drawl">drawl</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-Shapiro,_Peter_2005,_p._339_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shapiro,_Peter_2005,_p._339-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> notes his "drawled, <a href="/wiki/Laconic" class="mw-redirect" title="Laconic">laconic</a> rhyming" style.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_12-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kool_Moe_Dee" title="Kool Moe Dee">Kool Moe Dee</a> refers to Snoop's use of vocabulary, saying he "keeps it real simple...he simplifies it and he's effective in his simplicity".<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Broadus is known to <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap" title="Freestyle rap">freestyle</a> some of his lyrics on the spot&#160;– in the book <i><a href="/wiki/How_to_Rap" title="How to Rap">How to Rap</a>,</i> <a href="/wiki/Lady_of_Rage" class="mw-redirect" title="Lady of Rage">Lady of Rage</a> says, "When I worked with him earlier in his career, that's how created his stuff... he would freestyle, he wasn't a writer then, he was a freestyler",<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/The_D.O.C." title="The D.O.C.">The D.O.C.</a> states, "Snoop's [rap] was a one take willy, but his shit was all freestyle. He hadn't written nothing down. He just came in and started busting. The song was "Tha Shiznit"—that was all freestyle. He started busting and when we got to the break, Dre cut the machine off, did the chorus and told Snoop to come back in. He did that throughout the record. That's when Snoop was in the zone then."<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Peter_Shapiro_(journalist)" title="Peter Shapiro (journalist)">Peter Shapiro</a> says that Broadus debuted on "<a href="/wiki/Deep_Cover" title="Deep Cover">Deep Cover</a>" with a "shockingly original flow&#160;– which sounded like a <a href="/wiki/Slick_Rick" title="Slick Rick">Slick Rick</a> born in <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/South_London" title="South London">South London</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> and adds that he "showed where his style came from by covering <a href="/wiki/Slick_Rick" title="Slick Rick">Slick Rick</a>'s 'La Di Da Di'".<sup id="cite_ref-Shapiro,_Peter_2005,_p._339_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shapiro,_Peter_2005,_p._339-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Referring to Snoop's flow, <a href="/wiki/Kool_Moe_Dee" title="Kool Moe Dee">Kool Moe Dee</a> calls him "one of the smoothest, funkiest flow-ers in the game".<sup id="cite_ref-Kool_Moe_Dee_2003,_p.106_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kool_Moe_Dee_2003,_p.106-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/How_to_Rap" title="How to Rap">How to Rap</a></i> also notes that Snoop is known to use <a href="/wiki/Syncopation" title="Syncopation">syncopation</a> in his flow to give it a laidback quality,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> as well as 'linking with rhythm' in his <a href="/wiki/Compound_rhymes" class="mw-redirect" title="Compound rhymes">compound rhymes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> using <a href="/wiki/Alliteration" title="Alliteration">alliteration</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> and employing a "sparse" flow with good use of pauses.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Broadus listed his favorite rap albums for <i><a href="/wiki/Hip_Hop_Connection" title="Hip Hop Connection">Hip Hop Connection</a></i>:
10. Mixmaster Spade, <i>The Genius Is Back</i>
9. <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Miseducation_of_Lauryn_Hill" title="The Miseducation of Lauryn Hill">The Miseducation of Lauryn Hill</a></i>
8. <a href="/wiki/Ice_Cube" title="Ice Cube">Ice Cube</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Death_Certificate_(album)" title="Death Certificate (album)">Death Certificate</a></i>
7. <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">2Pac</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Me_Against_the_World" title="Me Against the World">Me Against the World</a></i>
6. <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ready_to_Die" title="Ready to Die">Ready to Die</a></i>
5. <a href="/wiki/N.W.A" title="N.W.A">N.W.A</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Straight_Outta_Compton" title="Straight Outta Compton">Straight Outta Compton</a></i>
4. <a href="/wiki/Eric_B._%26_Rakim" title="Eric B. &amp; Rakim">Eric B. &amp; Rakim</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Paid_in_Full_(album)" title="Paid in Full (album)">Paid in Full</a></i>
3. <a href="/wiki/Slick_Rick" title="Slick Rick">Slick Rick</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Adventures_of_Slick_Rick" title="The Great Adventures of Slick Rick">The Great Adventures of Slick Rick</a></i>
2. Snoop Doggy Dogg, <i><a href="/wiki/Doggystyle" title="Doggystyle">Doggystyle</a></i>
1. <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chronic" title="The Chronic">The Chronic</a></i> ("It's da illest shit")<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Snoop_Dogg_on_Stage.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Snoop_Dogg_on_Stage.jpg/170px-Snoop_Dogg_on_Stage.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Snoop_Dogg_on_Stage.jpg/255px-Snoop_Dogg_on_Stage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Snoop_Dogg_on_Stage.jpg/340px-Snoop_Dogg_on_Stage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2787" data-file-height="4180" /></a><figcaption>Snoop Dogg in August 2009</figcaption></figure>
<p>Snoop married his high school girlfriend, Shante Taylor, on June 14, 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> On May 21, 2004, he filed for divorce from Taylor, citing irreconcilable differences.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The couple however renewed vows on January 12, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> They have three children together: sons Cordé (born August 21, 1994) and Cordell (born February 21, 1997), who quit football to pursue a career as a film maker, and daughter Cori (born June 22, 1999).<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Snoop also has a son from a relationship with Laurie Holmond, Julian Corrie Broadus (born 1998). He is a first cousin of R&amp;B singers <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ray_J" title="Ray J">Ray J</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/New_Japan_Pro-Wrestling" title="New Japan Pro-Wrestling">NJPW</a> professional wrestler <a href="/wiki/Sasha_Banks" title="Sasha Banks">Sasha Banks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Snoop became a grandfather, as his eldest son, Cordé Broadus, had a son with his girlfriend, Jessica Kyzer.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Cordé had another son, who died on September 25, 2019, ten days after birth.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the start of his career, Snoop has been an avowed <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a> smoker, making it one of the trademarks of his image. In 2002, he announced he was giving up cannabis for good;<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> that did not last long (a situation famously referenced in the 2004 <a href="/wiki/Adam_Sandler" title="Adam Sandler">Adam Sandler</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/50_First_Dates" title="50 First Dates">50 First Dates</a></i>) and in 2013, he claimed to be smoking approximately 80 cannabis blunts a day.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> He has been certified for <a href="/wiki/Medical_cannabis" title="Medical cannabis">medical cannabis</a> in California to treat <a href="/wiki/Migraines" class="mw-redirect" title="Migraines">migraines</a> since at least 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Snoop claimed in a 2006 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine that unlike other hip hop artists who had superficially adopted the <a href="/wiki/Pimp" class="mw-redirect" title="Pimp">pimp</a> persona, he was an actual professional pimp in 2003 and 2004, saying, "That shit was my natural calling and once I got involved with it, it became fun. It was like shootin' layups for me. I was makin' 'em every time."
</p><p>On October 24, 2021, Snoop's mother, Beverly Tate, died.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<p>Snoop is an avid sports fan, including hometown teams <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers" title="Los Angeles Lakers">Los Angeles Lakers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/USC_Trojans_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="USC Trojans Football">USC Trojans</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> He has stated that he began following the Steelers in the 1970s while watching the team with his grandfather.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> He is also a fan of the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Raiders" title="Las Vegas Raiders">Las Vegas Raiders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Rams" title="Los Angeles Rams">Los Angeles Rams</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a>, often wearing a No. 5 jersey, and has been seen at Raiders training camps.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> He has shown affection for the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a>, having been seen performing at <a href="/wiki/Gillette_Stadium" title="Gillette Stadium">Gillette Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> He is an avid ice hockey fan,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> sporting jerseys from the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings" title="Los Angeles Kings">Los Angeles Kings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Penguins" title="Pittsburgh Penguins">Pittsburgh Penguins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Maple_Leafs" title="Toronto Maple Leafs">Toronto Maple Leafs</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Bruins" title="Boston Bruins">Boston Bruins</a> as well at the <a href="/wiki/American_Hockey_League" title="American Hockey League">AHL</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Springfield_Indians" title="Springfield Indians">Springfield Indians</a> in his 1994 music video "<a href="/wiki/Gin_and_Juice" title="Gin and Juice">Gin and Juice</a>". Snoop has been seen attending <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings" title="Los Angeles Kings">Los Angeles Kings</a> games. On his reality show <i><a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg%27s_Father_Hood" title="Snoop Dogg&#39;s Father Hood">Snoop Dogg's Father Hood</a>,</i> Snoop and his family received hockey lessons from the <a href="/wiki/Anaheim_Ducks" title="Anaheim Ducks">Anaheim Ducks</a>, then returned to the <a href="/wiki/Honda_Center" title="Honda Center">Honda Center</a> to cheer on the Ducks against the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Canucks" title="Vancouver Canucks">Vancouver Canucks</a> in the episode "Snow in da Hood".<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Snoop appeared in the video game <i><a href="/wiki/NHL_20" title="NHL 20">NHL 20</a></i> as both a guest commentator and a playable character in the "World of Chel" game mode.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Snoop is a certified football coach and has been head coach of his son Cordell's youth football teams.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Cordell played wide receiver and defensive back at <a href="/wiki/Bishop_Gorman_High_School" title="Bishop Gorman High School">Bishop Gorman High School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas, Nevada</a>, Cordell played on the 2014 state championship team, and received football <a href="/wiki/Athletic_scholarship" title="Athletic scholarship">scholarship</a> offers from <a href="/wiki/USC_Trojans_football" title="USC Trojans football">Southern California</a>, <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins_football" title="UCLA Bruins football">UCLA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies_football" title="Washington Huskies football">Washington</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_Golden_Bears_football" title="California Golden Bears football">Cal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon_State_Beavers_football" title="Oregon State Beavers football">Oregon State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_Blue_Devils_football" title="Duke Blue Devils football">Duke</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_football" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish football">Notre Dame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-YS110112_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YS110112-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Cordell committed and signed a letter of intent to play for <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins_football" title="UCLA Bruins football">UCLA</a> on February 4, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> On August 14, 2015, UCLA announced that Cordell had left the UCLA football team "to pursue other passions in his life".<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2022, Snoop signed with <a href="/wiki/Esports" title="Esports">esports</a> organization <a href="/wiki/FaZe_Clan" title="FaZe Clan">FaZe Clan</a> as board of directors and content creator.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In 2023, he resigned from the board of directors.<sup id="cite_ref-fazeres_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fazeres-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2005, Snoop Dogg has been operating a youth football league in the Los Angeles area.<sup id="cite_ref-Shilton_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shilton-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> He is a coach in the league, and one of the seasons he coached was documented in the <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Coach_Snoop" title="Coach Snoop">Coach Snoop</a></i>.
</p><p>As a 2023 <a href="/wiki/April_Fools%27_Day" title="April Fools&#39; Day">April Fools' Day</a> joke, the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a> announced that they had signed Snoop Dogg to the roster as a wide receiver.
</p><p>Snoop is a fan of <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic F.C.</a>, a football club based in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2023, he joined an investment group led by businessman Neko Sparks to help buy the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_Senators" title="Ottawa Senators">Ottawa Senators</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Shilton_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shilton-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<p>In 2009, it was reported that Snoop was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Nation_of_Islam" title="Nation of Islam">Nation of Islam</a>. On March 1, he made an appearance at the Nation of Islam's annual <a href="/wiki/Saviours%27_Day" title="Saviours&#39; Day">Saviours' Day</a> holiday, where he praised minister <a href="/wiki/Louis_Farrakhan" title="Louis Farrakhan">Louis Farrakhan</a>. Snoop said he was a member of the Nation, but declined to give the date on which he joined. He also donated $1,000 to the organization.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Claiming to be "born again" in 2012, Snoop <a href="/wiki/Religious_conversion" title="Religious conversion">converted</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Rastafari_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Rastafari movement">Rastafari movement</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> switched the focus of his music to reggae<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> and changed his name to Snoop Lion after a trip to Jamaica. He released a reggae album, <i>Reincarnated,</i> saying, "I have always said I was <a href="/wiki/Bob_Marley" title="Bob Marley">Bob Marley</a> reincarnated".<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2013, he was criticized by members of the Rastafari community in Jamaica, including reggae artist <a href="/wiki/Bunny_Wailer" title="Bunny Wailer">Bunny Wailer</a>, for alleged failure to meet his commitments to the culture.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Snoop later dismissed the claims, stating his beliefs were personal and not up for outside judgment.<sup id="cite_ref-Pearson_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pearson-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After releasing <i><a href="/wiki/Bible_of_Love" title="Bible of Love">Bible of Love</a></i> in early 2018 and performing in the <a href="/wiki/Stellar_Awards" title="Stellar Awards">33rd Annual Stellar Gospel Music Awards</a>, Snoop Dogg told a <a href="/wiki/TV_One_(American_TV_channel)" title="TV One (American TV channel)">TV One</a> interviewer while speaking of his Gospel influences that he "always referred to [his] savior <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesus Christ">Jesus Christ</a>" on most of his records, and that he had become "a <a href="/wiki/Born-again_Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Born-again Christian">born-again Christian</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity">Charity</span></h3>
<p>In 2005, Snoop Dogg founded the Snoop Youth Football League for at-risk youth in Southern California. In 2018, it was claimed to be the largest youth football organization in Southern California, with 50 teams and more than 1,500 players.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>  He has since claimed that at least 20 of his former pupils have gone on to play with the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nfl.com_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nfl.com-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Since 2017, he has also run a <a href="/wiki/Special_needs" title="Special needs">special-needs</a> division called Snoop Special Stars for anyone 5 years or older with a physical, mental, or developmental disability.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nfl.com_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nfl.com-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Snoop Dogg partners with city officials and annually gives away turkeys to the less fortunate in <a href="/wiki/Inglewood,_California" title="Inglewood, California">Inglewood, California</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving_(United_States)" title="Thanksgiving (United States)">Thanksgiving</a>. He gave away 3000 turkeys in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Broadus was also a judge for the 7th annual Independent Music Awards to support independent artists' careers.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although Snoop has donated and raised millions of dollars for charitable causes over the years, it is difficult to ascertain the full extent of Snoop's charitable giving, as he is wary that his donations and charitable causes might be seen as <a href="/wiki/Publicity_stunt" title="Publicity stunt">publicity stunts</a> for his own image. For example, regarding Snoop Special Stars, he said on <a href="/wiki/List_of_Sirius_XM_Radio_channels#Hip_hop" title="List of Sirius XM Radio channels">LL Cool J's <i>Rock the Bells Radio</i></a> that he avoided being in videos and photos at first—due to this apprehension—but he acquiesced once he saw the joy the kids and parents were getting by taking photos together.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Some other known causes that he supports include <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Hospital_Los_Angeles" title="Children&#39;s Hospital Los Angeles">Children's Hospital Los Angeles</a>, Mothers Against Police Brutality, <a href="/wiki/Habitat_for_Humanity" title="Habitat for Humanity">Habitat for Humanity</a>, Orca Network, Save a Life Foundation, <a href="/wiki/Shriners_Hospitals_for_Children" title="Shriners Hospitals for Children">Shriners Hospitals for Children</a>, and The Healing Circle.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Snoop_Dogg_speaking_at_press_conference.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Snoop_Dogg_speaking_at_press_conference.jpg/220px-Snoop_Dogg_speaking_at_press_conference.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Snoop_Dogg_speaking_at_press_conference.jpg/330px-Snoop_Dogg_speaking_at_press_conference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Snoop_Dogg_speaking_at_press_conference.jpg/440px-Snoop_Dogg_speaking_at_press_conference.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a><figcaption>Snoop Dogg and Los Angeles Mayor <a href="/wiki/Eric_Garcetti" title="Eric Garcetti">Eric Garcetti</a> speaking at a press conference following the <a href="/wiki/2016_shooting_of_Dallas_police_officers" title="2016 shooting of Dallas police officers">2016 shooting of Dallas police officers</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2012, Snoop Dogg endorsed Representative <a href="/wiki/Ron_Paul" title="Ron Paul">Ron Paul</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_Presidential_primaries,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Republican Party Presidential primaries, 2012">Republican presidential primary</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> but later said he would vote for <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2012_United_States_presidential_election" title="2012 United States presidential election">general election</a>, and on <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> gave ten reasons to vote for Obama (including "He a black nigga", "He's BFFs with <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Michelle_Obama" title="Michelle Obama">Michelle</a> got a fat ass"), and ten reasons not to vote for <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">Mitt Romney</a> (including "He a white nigga", "That muthafucka's name is Mitt", and "He a ho").<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 2013 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Huffington_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="The Huffington Post">The Huffington Post</a></i>, Snoop Dogg advocated for <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>, saying: "People can do what they want and as they please."<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his keynote address at the 2015 <a href="/wiki/South_by_Southwest" title="South by Southwest">South by Southwest</a> music festival, he blamed Los Angeles's explosion of gang violence in the 1980s on the economic policies of <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>, and insinuated that his administration shipped guns and drugs into the area.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He endorsed presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> on <a href="/wiki/Bravo_(American_TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bravo (American TV channel)">Bravo</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Watch_What_Happens_Live" class="mw-redirect" title="Watch What Happens Live">Watch What Happens Live</a></i> in May 2015, saying: "I would love to see a woman in office because I feel like we're at that stage in life to where we need a perspective other than the male's train of thought"<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> and "[...] just to have a woman speaking from a global perspective as far as representing America, I'd love to see that. So I'll be voting for Mrs. Clinton."<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following <a href="/wiki/2016_shooting_of_Dallas_police_officers" title="2016 shooting of Dallas police officers">the deadly shooting of five police officers in Dallas on July 7, 2016</a>, Snoop Dogg and <a href="/wiki/The_Game_(rapper)" title="The Game (rapper)">The Game</a> organized and led a peaceful march to the Los Angeles Police Department headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-Shakib-ap_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shakib-ap-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gomez-ap_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gomez-ap-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> The subsequent private meeting with the mayor Eric Garcetti and police chief Charlie Beck, and news conference was, according to Broadus, "[...] to get some dialogue and the communication going [...]".<sup id="cite_ref-abc-July-9-2016_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc-July-9-2016-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> The march and conference were part of an initiative called "Operation <abbr title="for both &quot;Hate Us Not Today&quot; and &quot;Hunt Us Not Today&quot;">H.U.N.T.</abbr>", serving as a police brutality protest in response to the police shooting and killing of two black men, <a href="/wiki/Philando_Castile" class="mw-redirect" title="Philando Castile">Philando Castile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alton_Sterling" class="mw-redirect" title="Alton Sterling">Alton Sterling</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ginsberg-hl_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ginsberg-hl-212">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> whose killing prompted nationwide protests including those that led to the Dallas killing of police officers. Broadus stated that "We are tired of what is going on and it's communication that is lacking".<sup id="cite_ref-abc-July-9-2016_211-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc-July-9-2016-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Reports of attendance range between 50–100 people.<sup id="cite_ref-Shakib-ap_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shakib-ap-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-abc-July-9-2016_211-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc-July-9-2016-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gomez-ap_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gomez-ap-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Poston-Rocha-Serna-Mather-latimes_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poston-Rocha-Serna-Mather-latimes-213">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Snoop Dogg advocates for the <a href="/wiki/Defund_the_police" title="Defund the police">defunding of police departments</a>, saying: "We need to start taking that money out of their pocket and put it back into our communities where we can police ourselves."<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Snoop has consistently expressed his support for tighter <a href="/wiki/Gun_control_after_the_Sandy_Hook_Elementary_School_shooting" title="Gun control after the Sandy Hook Elementary School shooting">gun control</a>. In 2013, then known as Snoop Lion, he told <a href="/wiki/HuffPost_Live" title="HuffPost Live">HuffPost Live</a>: "Politicians, you all got to pay attention, man. This world that we live in, it's so easy to get your hands on a gun. You've got to put some restrictions or ramifications on it. I can go outside right now and buy a gun. Easy. Just like that."<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, he released a song called "<a href="/wiki/No_Guns_Allowed" title="No Guns Allowed">No Guns Allowed</a>" feat. <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a> and Cori B in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, Snoop endorsed former Vice President <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> for President of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Animal_rights">Animal rights</span></h3>
<p>Snoop Dogg regularly appears in real <a href="/wiki/Fur" title="Fur">fur</a> garments, especially large coats, for which he attracts criticism from <a href="/wiki/Animal_welfare" title="Animal welfare">animal welfare</a> charities and younger audiences. In a <a href="/wiki/Video_podcast" class="mw-redirect" title="Video podcast">video podcast</a> in 2012, the rapper asked, "Why doesn't PETA throw paint on a pimp's fur coat".<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, Snoop Dogg claimed to have become a <a href="/wiki/Vegan" class="mw-redirect" title="Vegan">vegan</a>; however, he has since opted against a complete vegan diet.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> In June 2018, he performed at the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Media_Association" title="Environmental Media Association">Environmental Media Association</a> (EMA) Honors Gala. While he was performing, the logo for vegan brand <a href="/wiki/Beyond_Meat" title="Beyond Meat">Beyond Meat</a> was displayed on the screens behind him.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, Snoop Dogg invested in vegan food company Original Foods, which makes Pigless Pork Rinds, which he has said are a favorite.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> He is an ambassador for Beyond Meat and lent his name and image as well as financial support for Beyond Meat's Feed a Million+ campaign to provide a million frontline workers with Beyond Meat burgers.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_records">World records</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_paradise_cocktail">Largest paradise cocktail</span></h3>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/BottleRock_Napa_Valley" title="BottleRock Napa Valley">BottleRock Napa Valley</a> music festival on May 26, 2018, Snoop Dogg, <a href="/wiki/Warren_G" title="Warren G">Warren G</a>, Kendall Coleman, Kim Kaechele, and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Voltaggio" title="Michael Voltaggio">Michael Voltaggio</a> set the <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Record</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Paradise_(cocktail)#In_popular_culture" title="Paradise (cocktail)">largest paradise cocktail</a>. Measuring 550 liters (150&#160;U.S.&#160;gal), the "Gin and Juice" drink was mixed from 180 1.75-liter (0.46&#160;U.S.&#160;gal) bottles of <a href="/wiki/Gin" title="Gin">gin</a>, 156 1-liter (0.26&#160;U.S.&#160;gal) bottles of <a href="/wiki/Apricot_brandy" title="Apricot brandy">apricot brandy</a> and 28 1-U.S.-gallon (3.8&#160;L) jugs of <a href="/wiki/Orange_juice" title="Orange juice">orange juice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GWR,_world_record,_gin_and_juice_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GWR,_world_record,_gin_and_juice-225">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reported_volume_and_content">Reported volume and content</span></h4>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> reported its total volume as "...more than 132 gallons [500&#160;L], according to Guinness...", following with an embedded <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweet</a> by Liam Mayclem via GWR (the Guinness World Records' official Twitter account), showing a reply from GWR to its own tweet stating "[t]he cocktail contained 180 bottles of Hendricks gin, 154 bottles of apricot brandy and 38 3.78 litre jugs of orange juice..."<sup id="cite_ref-time,_world_record,_gin_and_juice_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time,_world_record,_gin_and_juice-226">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Mixmag" title="Mixmag">Mixmag</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> published the same content quantities as GWR's tweet.<sup id="cite_ref-mixmag,_world_record,_gin_and_juice_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mixmag,_world_record,_gin_and_juice-227">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NME,_world_record,_gin_and_juice_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NME,_world_record,_gin_and_juice-228">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USA_Today,_world_record,_gin_and_juice_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USA_Today,_world_record,_gin_and_juice-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> with <i>Mixmag</i> reporting that "[a]ccording to Guinness the cocktail measured at 132 gallons."<sup id="cite_ref-mixmag,_world_record,_gin_and_juice_227-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mixmag,_world_record,_gin_and_juice-227">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> <i>NME</i> states that the total volume was "...more than 132 gallons"<sup id="cite_ref-NME,_world_record,_gin_and_juice_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NME,_world_record,_gin_and_juice-228">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> and <i>USA Today</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> European website states that "[a] Guinness World Records official was on hand to certify the record of the 550 liter cocktail."<sup id="cite_ref-USA_Today,_world_record,_gin_and_juice_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USA_Today,_world_record,_gin_and_juice-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> published that "...the concoction required 180 handles of Hendricks gin, resulting in a gigantic beverage...".<sup id="cite_ref-billboard,_world_record,_gin_and_juice_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard,_world_record,_gin_and_juice-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_incidents">Legal incidents</span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Snoop_Dogg_mugshot.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Snoop_Dogg_mugshot.jpg/170px-Snoop_Dogg_mugshot.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="212" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Snoop_Dogg_mugshot.jpg/255px-Snoop_Dogg_mugshot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Snoop_Dogg_mugshot.jpg/340px-Snoop_Dogg_mugshot.jpg 2x" data-file-width="739" data-file-height="920" /></a><figcaption>Mug shot (1993)</figcaption></figure>
<p>Shortly after graduating from high school in 1989, Broadus was arrested for possession of <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a> and for the following three years was frequently in and out of prison.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicbio_12-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicbio-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1990, he was convicted of felony possession of drugs and possession for sale.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes27apr2007_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes27apr2007-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While recording <i>Doggystyle</i> in August 1993, Broadus was arrested in connection with the death of a member of a rival gang who was allegedly shot and killed by Broadus's bodyguard; Broadus had been temporarily living in an apartment complex in the <a href="/wiki/Palms,_Los_Angeles" title="Palms, Los Angeles">Palms</a> neighborhood in the <a href="/wiki/Westside,_Los_Angeles" class="mw-redirect" title="Westside, Los Angeles">West Los Angeles</a> region, in the intersection of Vinton Avenue and Woodbine Street—the location of the shooting. Both men were charged with murder, as Broadus was purportedly driving the vehicle from which the gun was fired. <a href="/wiki/Johnnie_Cochran" title="Johnnie Cochran">Johnnie Cochran</a> defended them.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> Both Broadus and his bodyguard were acquitted on February 20, 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 1993, Broadus was stopped for a traffic violation, and a firearm was found by police during a search of his car. In February 1997, he pled guilty to possession of a handgun and was ordered to record three public service announcements, perform 800 hours of community service, pay a $1,000 fine and serve three years' probation.<sup id="cite_ref-Los_Angeles_County_District_Attorneys_Office_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Los_Angeles_County_District_Attorneys_Office-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Weapons_charge_2007_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weapons_charge_2007-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2006, Broadus was detained at <a href="/wiki/John_Wayne_Airport" title="John Wayne Airport">John Wayne Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County, California</a>, by airport security after airport screeners found a collapsible police <a href="/wiki/Baton_(law_enforcement)" title="Baton (law enforcement)">baton</a> in his carry-on bag. Donald Etra, Broadus's lawyer, told deputies the baton was a prop for a musical sketch. Broadus was sentenced to three years' probation and 160 hours of community service for the incident, starting in September 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> He was arrested again in October 2006 at <a href="/wiki/Bob_Hope_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Hope Airport">Bob Hope Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Burbank,_California" title="Burbank, California">Burbank</a> after being stopped for a traffic infraction; he was arrested for possession of a firearm and for suspicion of transporting an unspecified amount of marijuana, according to a police statement.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> The following month, after taping an appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno" title="The Tonight Show with Jay Leno">The Tonight Show with Jay Leno</a>,</i> he was arrested again for possession of <a href="/wiki/Marijuana" class="mw-redirect" title="Marijuana">marijuana</a>, cocaine and a firearm. Two members of his entourage, according to the Burbank police statement, were admitted members of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rollin_20&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rollin 20 (page does not exist)">Rollin 20</a>'s Crips gang and were arrested on separate charges.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> In April 2007 he was given a three-year <a href="/wiki/Suspended_sentence" title="Suspended sentence">suspended sentence</a>, five years' probation and 800 hours of community service after pleading <a href="/wiki/No_contest" class="mw-redirect" title="No contest">no contest</a> to two felony charges of drug and gun possession by a convicted felon. He was also prohibited from hiring anyone with a criminal record or gang affiliation as a security guard or driver.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes27apr2007_231-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes27apr2007-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 26, 2006, Broadus and members of his entourage were arrested after being turned away from <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>' first class lounge at <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a> in London. Broadus and his party were denied entry to the lounge due to some members flying in economy class. After being escorted outside, the group got in a fight with the police and vandalized a <a href="/wiki/Duty-free_shop" title="Duty-free shop">duty-free shop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Seven police officers were injured during the incident. After a night in jail, Broadus and the other men were released on bail the next day but he was unable to perform a scheduled concert in <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> On May 15 the <a href="/wiki/Home_Office" title="Home Office">Home Office</a> decided that he would be denied entry to the United Kingdom for the foreseeable future and his British visa was denied the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> As of March 2010, however, Broadus was allowed back into the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-rapbasement.com_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rapbasement.com-245">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> The entire group was banned from British Airways "for the foreseeable future".<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> According to Broadus, none other than <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> herself overturned the ban, saying: "This man has done nothing in our country. He can come."<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2007, the Australian <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Immigration_and_Citizenship_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Immigration and Citizenship (Australia)">Department of Immigration and Citizenship</a> banned him from entering the country on character grounds, citing his prior criminal convictions.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> He had been scheduled to appear at the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Australia_Video_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Australia Video Music Awards">MTV Australia Video Music Awards</a> on <a href="/wiki/MTV_Australia_Video_Music_Awards_2007" title="MTV Australia Video Music Awards 2007">April 29, 2007</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> The Australian <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Immigration_and_Citizenship_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Immigration and Citizenship (Australia)">Department of Immigration and Citizenship</a> lifted the ban in September 2008 and had granted him a visa to tour Australia. The DIAC said: "In making this decision, the department weighed his criminal convictions against his previous behaviour while in Australia, recent conduct&#160;– including charity work&#160;– and any likely risk to the Australian community ... We took into account all relevant factors and, on balance, the department decided to grant the visa."<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Broadus was banned from entering Norway for two years in July 2012 after entering the country the month before in possession of 8 grams (0.3&#160;oz) of marijuana and an undeclared 227,000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Norwegian_crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian crown">kr</a> in cash, or about US$29,400 in 2022 terms.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC20120729_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC20120729-254">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Snoop Dogg, after performing for a concert in <a href="/wiki/Uppsala" title="Uppsala">Uppsala</a>, Sweden, on July 25, 2015, was pulled over and detained by Swedish police for allegedly using illegal drugs, violating a Swedish law enacted in 1988 which criminalized the recreational use of such substances – therefore making even being under the influence of any illegal/controlled substance a crime itself without possession. During the detention he was taken to the police station to perform a drug test and was released shortly afterwards. The rapid test was positive for traces of narcotics and he was potentially subject to fines depending on the results of more detailed analysis.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> Although final results "strongly" indicated drug use the charges were ultimately dropped because it could not be proven that he was in Sweden when he consumed the substances.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> The rapper uploaded several videos on the social networking site <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> criticizing the police for alleged <a href="/wiki/Racial_profiling" title="Racial profiling">racial profiling</a>; police spokesman Daniel Nilsson responded to the accusations, saying: "we don't work like that in Sweden." He declared in the videos, "Niggas got me in the back of police car right now in Sweden, cuz," and "Pulled a nigga over for nothing, taking us to the station where I've got to go pee in a cup for nothin'. I ain't done nothin'. All I did was came to the country and did a concert and now I've got to go to the police station. For nothin'!" He announced to his Swedish fanbase that he would no longer go on tour in the country due to the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Snoop Dogg has also been arrested and fined three times for misdemeanor possession of marijuana: in Los Angeles in 1998;<sup id="cite_ref-articles.latimes.com_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-articles.latimes.com-263">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a>, Ohio in 2001;<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Blanca,_Texas" title="Sierra Blanca, Texas">Sierra Blanca, Texas</a>, in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the Death Row Records bankruptcy case, Snoop Dogg lost $2 million.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2022, a woman sued Snoop Dogg for $10 million, alleging that he <a href="/wiki/Sexual_assault" title="Sexual assault">sexually assaulted</a> her in May 2013 following a concert in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">Anaheim, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> A source representing Snoop Dogg has denied the accusation.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> Snoop Dogg was also sued for sexual assault in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmography">Filmography</span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg_filmography" title="Snoop Dogg filmography">Snoop Dogg filmography</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_legacy">Awards and legacy</span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Snoop_Dogg" title="List of awards and nominations received by Snoop Dogg">List of awards and nominations received by Snoop Dogg</a></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>,  and <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> have called him a "<a href="/wiki/West_Coast_hip_hop" title="West Coast hip hop">West Coast</a> icon";<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Press-Telegram" title="Press-Telegram">Press-Telegram</a></i>, "an icon of gangsta rap".<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)"><i>Vibe</i> magazine</a> called him "The King of the West Coast".<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a> journalist Paul Donoughue, cited him among the 1990s acts that took hip-hop into the pop music charts.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> Broadus received the <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_Music,_Inc." title="Broadcast Music, Inc.">BMI</a> Icon Award in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> In 2023, he was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">Songwriters Hall of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Broadus popularized the use of <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-izzle" class="extiw" title="wikt:-izzle">-izzle speak</a></i> particularly in the pop and hip-hop music industry.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> A type of <a href="/wiki/Infix" title="Infix">infix</a>, it first found popularity when used by <a href="/wiki/Frankie_Smith" title="Frankie Smith">Frankie Smith</a> in his 1981 hit song "<a href="/wiki/Double_Dutch_Bus" title="Double Dutch Bus">Double Dutch Bus</a>". 
<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> Rob Fitzpatrick has credited his album <i>Doggystyle</i> for proving that rappers "could reinvent themselves", expanding rap's vocabulary, changing hip-hop fashions, and helping introduce a hip-hop genre called <a href="/wiki/G-funk" title="G-funk">G-funk</a> to a new generation.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> The album has been cited as an influence by rapper <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> while fellow rappers <a href="/wiki/ScHoolboy_Q" class="mw-redirect" title="ScHoolboy Q">ScHoolboy Q</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maxo_Kream" title="Maxo Kream">Maxo Kream</a> have also cited him as an influence.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

Other names that he has released music under include "DJ Snoopadelic", "Snoopzilla", "Bigg Snoop Dogg", and simply "Snoop".</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
